# Investigation: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

**Repository:** prometheus/prometheus
**Task Type:** Cross-Service Debug (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After a Prometheus upgrade, remote-write destinations intermittently stop receiving samples. The issue correlates with target discovery changes — when targets are added or removed, some remote-write shards stall.

Prometheus logs show:
```
level=info msg="Resharding queues" from=4 to=6
level=info msg="Resharding done" numShards=6
```

But after resharding, metrics show some shards have `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. How remote-write queue resharding works (which files/functions)
2. What changed in the resharding logic recently
3. The specific mechanism causing shards to stall
4. Why the issue is intermittent (timing/race condition)
5. Which metrics or logs would confirm the root cause

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `storage/remote/` package, particularly queue management and shard calculation

  1378→func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {

  1389→		// the batch being processed.

  1307→// enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or
  1308→// resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and
  1309→// retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,
  1310→// specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the
  1311→// partial batch has also been filled.
  1312→func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {
  1313→	s.mtx.RLock()
  1314→	defer s.mtx.RUnlock()
  1315→	shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))
  1316→	select {
  1317→	case <-s.softShutdown:
  1318→		return false
  1319→	default:
  1320→		appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)
  1321→		if !appended {
  1322→			return false
  1323→		}
  1324→		switch data.sType {
  1325→		case tSample:
  1326→			s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()
  1327→			s.enqueuedSamples.Inc()
  1328→		case tExemplar:
  1329→			s.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()
  1330→			s.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()
  1331→		case tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:
  1332→			s.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()
  1333→			s.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()
  1334→		default:
  1335→			return true
  1336→		}

101-assistanttext-
The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

**Key findings:**

Commit `184c7eb` moved `dataIn` rate tracking from `WriteStorage.timestampTracker.Commit()` (appender level, always runs) into `shards.enqueue()` (only incremented on successful enqueue). During resharding, `enqueue()` returns `false` because `softShutdown` is closed or queues are full, so `dataIn` stops accumulating. The EWMA rate decays toward zero, causing `calculateDesiredShards()` to undercount needed shards. This creates a feedback loop where:

1. Resharding triggers stop/start of shards
2. During stop, enqueue fails → `dataIn` stops incrementing
3. EWMA decays → `calculateDesiredShards()` sees low incoming rate
4. Shards either stall (pending data stuck) or oscillate between shard counts
5. The problem is intermittent because it depends on queues being full and remote endpoint latency

The same commit also removed `dataDropped` from the shard formula, causing over-estimation of needed shards when relabeling drops series, triggering unnecessary reshards that amplify the stall.

This was already identified and fixed on `release-3.7` by reverting both commits in `6806b68`.

41. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Investigation Report\n\n## Summary\n\nCommit `184c7eb` (\"storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level\") moved the `dataIn` EWMA rate tracking from the `WriteStorage` level (via `timestampTracker.Commit()`) into the `shards.enqueue()` method, and also removed the `dataDropped` tracking from the shard calculation. This causes a deadlock/stall during resharding: when shards are stopped and restarted, the `enqueue()` call returns `false` (because `softShutdown` is closed), so `dataIn` stops accumulating. When new shards start with empty queues, the shard calculation sees `dataInRate` drop toward zero, preventing proper upscaling. Additionally, the removal of `dataDropped` from the shard calculation inflates the desired shard count when relabeling drops series, causing unnecessary resharding that triggers the stall.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause involves two interrelated problems introduced by commit `184c7eb9186aa8fea09920f2f8e8aa8a603da300`:\n\n### Problem 1: `dataIn` moved into `enqueue()` creates a resharding deadlock\n\n**Before the change (working code):**\n- `dataIn` was an `*ewmaRate` shared across all `QueueManager` instances, owned by `WriteStorage`\n- It was incremented in `timestampTracker.Commit()` (`storage/remote/write.go:346`) \u2014 i.e., at the storage appender level, *before* any queue/shard interaction\n- It was ticked by a goroutine in `WriteStorage.run()` independently of shard state\n- This meant `dataIn.rate()` always reflected the true incoming data rate regardless of shard lifecycle\n\n**After the change (broken code):**\n- `dataIn` became a per-`QueueManager` `*ewmaRate` created locally (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:515`)\n- It is now incremented inside `shards.enqueue()` (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1338`)\n- It is ticked inside `calculateDesiredShards()` (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1112`)\n\nThe critical problem: during resharding, `reshardLoop()` calls `t.shards.stop()` then `t.shards.start(numShards)` (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1236-1237`). When `stop()` is called:\n\n1. `softShutdown` channel is closed (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1275`)\n2. All calls to `enqueue()` now hit the `case <-s.softShutdown: return false` path (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1317-1318`)\n3. The `Append()` method retries with backoff (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:756-780`) but `enqueue()` keeps returning `false` during the entire stop/start transition\n4. Since `dataIn.incr(1)` is only called on successful enqueue (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1338`), **no data is counted as \"incoming\" during resharding**\n5. When shards are full (capacity exhausted), `enqueue()` returns `false` even before `softShutdown` because `queue.Append()` returns `false` when the `batchQueue` channel is full (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1447-1454`)\n\nWhen `stop()` blocks waiting for in-flight RPCs (which is common with slow remote endpoints), and the queues were already full prior to resharding, the system enters a state where:\n- `dataIn` stops accumulating because enqueue fails\n- The EWMA rate decays toward zero on subsequent ticks\n- `calculateDesiredShards()` sees low `dataInRate` and calculates fewer desired shards\n- This prevents upscaling even though the actual incoming data rate is high\n- Pending samples remain stuck in the old queues being drained, showing `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0\n\n### Problem 2: Removal of `dataDropped` inflates shard calculation\n\nThe same commit removed the `dataDropped` EWMA entirely from the shard calculation. Previously, the formula was:\n\n```\ndataKeptRatio = dataOutRate / (dataDropped.rate() + dataOutRate)\ndesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate * dataKeptRatio + backlogCatchup)\n```\n\nAfter the change:\n```\ndesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n```\n\nWhen write-relabel configs drop a significant portion of series, the old code correctly accounted for this \u2014 the dropped data shouldn't be counted toward shard need. The new code treats all incoming data as needing shards, **overestimating** desired shards. This causes unnecessary upscaling reshards, which when combined with Problem 1, triggers the stall more frequently.\n\n### Why it's intermittent\n\nThe stall depends on precise timing:\n1. A target discovery change triggers recalculation of desired shards\n2. The resharding decision coincides with queues being near-full (high pending count)\n3. `shards.stop()` takes significant time because `FlushAndShutdown` waits for in-flight RPCs up to `flushDeadline` (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1289`)\n4. During this window, `dataIn` decays because no enqueues succeed\n5. After `shards.start()`, the new shard count may be wrong (too low) or the EWMA rate needs multiple ticks (10s each) to recover to reflect actual load\n6. If the remote endpoint is slow (high latency), RPCs take longer, making the stop phase longer, making the stall more likely\n\nThe issue does NOT occur if:\n- Queues are not full when resharding happens (enqueue succeeds quickly with new shards)\n- The remote endpoint is fast (stop phase is short)\n- No relabeling drops series (dataDropped removal doesn't matter)\n- Target count is stable (no resharding triggered)\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Commit introducing the bug\n- `184c7eb9186aa8fea09920f2f8e8aa8a603da300` \u2014 \"storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level\"\n\n### Key code changes in 184c7eb\n\n1. **`dataIn` moved into `enqueue()`**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1338` \u2014 `s.qm.dataIn.incr(1)` only called on *successful* enqueue\n2. **`dataIn` no longer shared**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:515` \u2014 `dataIn: newEWMARate(ewmaWeight, shardUpdateDuration)` (per-QueueManager, not shared)\n3. **`dataDropped` removed**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:455` \u2014 `dataIn, dataOut, dataOutDuration *ewmaRate` (no `dataDropped`)\n4. **`dataKeptRatio` removed from calculation**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1124` \u2014 `dataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate` (was `dataInRate*dataKeptRatio - dataOutRate`)\n5. **`dataIn.tick()` moved**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1112` \u2014 now ticked in `calculateDesiredShards()` instead of a dedicated goroutine in `WriteStorage.run()`\n\n### Fix commit (on release-3.7 branch)\n- `6806b68f930722746b23f3e30f184b22ca1fafe0` \u2014 \"[release-3.7] fix: Remote-write: revert changes in the queue resharding logic (#17412)\"\n- Reverts both `184c7eb` and `ba14bc49d`, restoring `dataIn` to `WriteStorage` level, bringing back `dataDropped`, and adding a test `TestRemoteWrite_ReshardingWithoutDeadlock`\n\n### Critical code paths\n\n- **Resharding loop**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1183-1198` (`reshardLoop`) \u2014 calls `stop()` then `start()`\n- **Stop blocks on flush**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1268-1305` (`shards.stop()`) \u2014 waits up to `flushDeadline`\n- **Enqueue fails during stop**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1316-1318` \u2014 `softShutdown` check returns `false`\n- **Append retries on false**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:756-780` \u2014 busy loop with backoff on enqueue failure\n- **Shard calculation**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1111-1175` (`calculateDesiredShards`) \u2014 uses `dataIn.rate()` which decays to zero during resharding\n- **pendingSamples reset to 0**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1241` \u2014 `start()` resets pending counter but old shard goroutines may still have data\n\n### Related GitHub issue\n- The fix commit references issue #17384 in its test: `TestRemoteWrite_ReshardingWithoutDeadlock`\n\n## Affected Components\n\n- **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`** \u2014 `QueueManager`, `shards`, `calculateDesiredShards()`, `reshardLoop()`, `enqueue()`\n- **`storage/remote/write.go`** \u2014 `WriteStorage`, `timestampTracker.Commit()`\n- **`storage/remote/ewma.go`** \u2014 `ewmaRate` (EWMA rate tracker used for `dataIn`, `dataOut`, `dataDropped`)\n- **`storage/remote/max_timestamp.go`** \u2014 `maxTimestamp` (used for `highestTimestamp`, `highestRecvTimestamp`)\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix is to revert commits `184c7eb` and `ba14bc49d`, which has already been done on the `release-3.7` branch in commit `6806b68`. Specifically:\n\n1. **Move `dataIn` tracking back to `WriteStorage` level**: `dataIn` should be incremented in `timestampTracker.Commit()` (before queueing), not in `shards.enqueue()`. This ensures the incoming data rate is always tracked regardless of shard state.\n\n2. **Restore `dataDropped` EWMA**: The `dataKeptRatio` calculation prevents over-counting when relabeling drops series, avoiding unnecessary reshards.\n\n3. **Restore shared `samplesIn` EWMA**: Having a single `samplesIn` ticked by a dedicated goroutine in `WriteStorage.run()` ensures consistent tick intervals independent of shard lifecycle.\n\n4. **Restore `highestRecvTimestamp` at `WriteStorage` level**: Keep the received timestamp tracking at the appender level, not inside enqueue.\n\n### Diagnostic Steps to Confirm Root Cause\n\n1. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired`**: After resharding events, does this metric drop suddenly? If `dataInRate` collapses during resharding, desired shards will drop.\n\n2. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`**: If stuck at >0 and not progressing, confirms shards stalled after resharding.\n\n3. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total`**: A spike in retries during resharding confirms enqueue failures, which means `dataIn` is not being incremented.\n\n4. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_timestamp_seconds` vs `prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_sent_timestamp_seconds`**: An increasing gap after resharding events confirms data is not being sent.\n\n5. **Correlate with `prometheus_remote_storage_shards`**: Look for the pattern: resharding increases shards -> stall -> next calculation decreases shards (because `dataInRate` decayed) -> another reshard -> more stall.\n\n6. **Enable debug logging**: Look for `\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\"` log entries showing `dataInRate=0` or near-zero values during/after resharding events.\n",

Specifically:\n\n1. **Move `dataIn` tracking back to `WriteStorage` level**: `dataIn` should be incremented in `timestampTracker.Commit()` (before queueing), not in `shards.enqueue()`. This ensures the incoming data rate is always tracked regardless of shard state.\n\n2. **Restore `dataDropped` EWMA**: The `dataKeptRatio` calculation prevents over-counting when relabeling drops series, avoiding unnecessary reshards.\n\n3. **Restore shared `samplesIn` EWMA**: Having a single `samplesIn` ticked by a dedicated goroutine in `WriteStorage.run()` ensures consistent tick intervals independent of shard lifecycle.\n\n4. **Restore `highestRecvTimestamp` at `WriteStorage` level**: Keep the received timestamp tracking at the appender level, not inside enqueue.\n\n### Diagnostic Steps to Confirm Root Cause\n\n1. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired`**: After resharding events, does this metric drop suddenly? If `dataInRate` collapses during resharding, desired shards will drop.\n\n2. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`**: If stuck at >0 and not progressing, confirms shards stalled after resharding.\n\n3. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total`**: A spike in retries during resharding confirms enqueue failures, which means `dataIn` is not being incremented.\n\n4. **Check `prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_timestamp_seconds` vs `prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_sent_timestamp_seconds`**: An increasing gap after resharding events confirms data is not being sent.\n\n5. **Correlate with `prometheus_remote_storage_shards`**: Look for the pattern: resharding increases shards -> stall -> next calculation decreases shards (because `dataInRate` decayed) -> another reshard -> more stall.\n\n6. **Enable debug logging**: Look for `\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\"` log entries showing `dataInRate=0` or near-zero values during/after resharding events.\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Investigation Report

## Summary

Commit `184c7eb` ("storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level") moved the `dataIn` EWMA rate tracking from the `WriteStorage` level (via `timestampTracker.Commit()`) into the `shards.enqueue()` method, and also removed the `dataDropped` tracking from the shard calculation. This causes a deadlock/stall during resharding: when shards are stopped and restarted, the `enqueue()` call returns `false` (because `softShutdown` is closed), so `dataIn` stops accumulating. When new shards start with empty queues, the shard calculation sees `dataInRate` drop toward zero, preventing proper upscaling. Additionally, the removal of `dataDropped` from the shard calculation inflates the desired shard count when relabeling drops series, causing unnecessary resharding that triggers the stall.

## Root Cause

The root cause involves two interrelated problems introduced by commit `184c7eb9186aa8fea09920f2f8e8aa8a603da300`:

### Problem 1: `dataIn` moved into `enqueue()` creates a resharding deadlock

**Before the change (working code):**
- `dataIn` was an `*ewmaRate` shared across all `QueueManager` instances, owned by `WriteStorage`
- It was incremented in `timestampTracker.Commit()` (`storage/remote/write.go:346`) — i.e., at the storage appender level, *before* any queue/shard interaction
- It was ticked by a goroutine in `WriteStorage.run()` independently of shard state
- This meant `dataIn.rate()` always reflected the true incoming data rate regardless of shard lifecycle

**After the change (broken code):**
- `dataIn` became a per-`QueueManager` `*ewmaRate` created locally (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:515`)
- It is now incremented inside `shards.enqueue()` (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1338`)
- It is ticked inside
... (truncated)
